[Thinking] Excellent! The oh-my-pi research agent has provided a very detailed report. The key takeaways for jcode:

   - Top border: `┌────────────────────┐` in bashMode color (#00ff88)
   - `$ command` in bold, border color

Let me trace the bug:

When the user is at "History 2" (meaning there are 2 prompts, and they haven't navigated yet):
- `nav_pos` should be 0 (not navigating)
- `nav_total` should be... well, `prompt_history_info` returns `None` when not navigating
- So it falls through to `let total = app.display_user_message_count() + pending_count;` which gives "2"

- `visible_prompt_history` returns all user messages

Wait, looking at my implementation:
```rust
fn prompt_history_info(&self) -> Option<(usize, usize)> {
    let history = super::input::visible_prompt_history(self);
    if history.is_empty() {
        return None;
    }
    let current = self.input.trim();
    history.iter().rposition(|p| p == current).map(|pos| (pos + 1, history.len()))
}
```

The issue is with the history list ordering. `visible_prompt_history` returns messages from the DISPLAY (which is in order from oldest to newest). `rposition` finds the LAST matching item from the END of the list.

When the user has 2 prompts:
- History = ["first prompt", "second prompt"]
- Current input = "second prompt" (just typed, not navigated yet)
- `rposition` finds the LAST occurrence → index 1 → pos+1 = 2 → "2/2" ✅

When user presses UP:
- Current input = "first prompt" (navigated to previous)
- `rposition` finds the LAST occurrence → index 0 → pos+1 = 1 → "1/2" ✅

Wait, that should be correct! "History 1/2" when on the first prompt. But the user says it shows "History 1/1".

pub(super) fn visible_prompt_history(app: &App) -> Vec<String> {

        .iter()
        .filter(|message| message.role == "user")
        .map(|message| message.content.trim().to_string())
        .filter(|content| !content.is_empty())
        .collect()
}
```

This collects ALL user messages. When the user has typed the same prompt twice (e.g., two identical messages), `rposition` finds the LAST match. But the LAST match is the CURRENT message (the one they just typed before pressing UP). When they press UP, the current input becomes the PREVIOUS message. But `rposition` still finds... 

Wait, I think the real issue is: after navigating to a history item, the current input becomes that history item's text. `rposition` from the END finds the LAST occurrence of that text in history. If the user typed the same text twice (e.g., two messages with the same content), `rposition` would find the SECOND occurrence (the most recent one), making `pos+1` = 2 instead of 1.

`feb425b5` pushed. Status bar **3 layers** complete:

**Layer 3 — Custom shell command** (Claude Code style):
```toml
[status_line]
command = "echo '$(date +%H:%M) | $(whoami)'"
```

Khi set `status_line.command`, jcode spawn shell command, pipe JSON stdin (model, provider, context, permission mode), render stdout làm status line. Nếu command fail → fallback về built-in.

Cách dùng:
```bash
/set status_line.command "echo 'model is $(jcode info --model)'"
/statusline on
```

Hoặc viết script `.sh` / `.mjs` để render custom status line với đầy đủ thông tin.

Tổng kết toàn bộ status bar:

| Layer | File | Status |
|-------|------|--------|
| **1. Built-in** | `ui_input.rs` → `status_line_text()` | ✅ model + provider + context bar + tokens |
| **2. `/statusline`** | `commands.rs` + `config_file.rs` | ✅ on/off/setup |
| **3. Shell command** | `ui_input.rs` → `run_custom_command()` | ✅ stdin JSON, stdout render |

[Tool: read]

> 1|---  
> 2|name: feature-planning  
> 3|description: >  
> 4|  Deep feature research and implementation planning for AI coding agent projects. Use this skill  
> 5|  whenever a user asks about a feature they want to implement, improve, add, or design — especially  
> 6|  in the context of AI coding agents, CLI tools, terminal agents, or LLM-powered developer tools.  
> 7|  Triggers on: "I want to add X feature", "how do I implement X", "can we improve X", "I want to  
> 8|  build X into my agent", "feature request for X", "how does X work in these tools", or any phrasing  
> 9|  that implies implementing/improving a capability. This skill clones 7 reference repos, spawns  
> 10|  sub-agents for deep per-repo research, runs an ultra-QA interview with the user, then produces a  
> 11|  comprehensive implementation plan with code, pseudocode, test cases, benchmarks, and direct repo  
> 12|  links — so the user can go from idea to working implementation with total confidence.  
> 13|---  
> 14|  
> 15|# Feature Planning Skill  
> 16|  
> 17|Comprehensive feature research + implementation planning using 9 reference repos as the knowledge base.  
> 18|  
> 19|## Reference Repositories  
> 20|  
> 21|| Alias | Repo URL | Stack | What it teaches |  
> 22||-------|----------|-------|-----------------|  
> 23|| `oh-my-openagent` | https://github.com/code-yeongyu/oh-my-openagent | TypeScript / OpenCode plugin | Multi-agent orchestration, model routing, tmux sessions, delegate-task patterns |  
> 24|| `opencode` | https://github.com/anomalyco/opencode | TypeScript / Bun monorepo | Open-source AI coding agent architecture, provider abstraction, TUI |  
> 25|| `oh-my-pi` | https://github.com/can1357/oh-my-pi | TypeScript + Rust / Bun | 40+ providers, 32 tools, LSP+DAP ops, benchmarked edits, IDE wiring |  
> 26|| `codebuff` | https://github.com/CodebuffAI/codebuff | TypeScript / multi-agent | File picker + planner + editor + reviewer pipeline, beats Claude Code on evals |  
> 27|| `codex` | https://github.com/openai/codex | TypeScript / Node | OpenAI Codex CLI, sandboxed execution, hardened tool use |

> 29|| `pi-agent-rust` | https://github.com/Dicklesworthstone/pi_agent_rust | Rust 2024 edition | High-perf Rust agent, SQLite sessions, SSE streaming, WASM extension security |  
> 30|| `oh-my-claudecode` | https://github.com/Yeachan-Heo/oh-my-claudecode | TypeScript / Claude Code plugin | Claude Code extension with hooks, guards, permission modes, multi-agent tools |  
> 31|| `oh-my-codex` | https://github.com/Yeachan-Heo/oh-my-codex | TypeScript / Codex plugin | Codex extension with approval modes, sandbox config, tool gating |  
> 32|  
> 33|---  
> 34|  
> 35|## Workflow (follow this order every time)  
> 36|  
> 37|### Phase 1 — Clone & Sub-agent Research  
> 38|  
> 39|When the skill is triggered, immediately clone all 9 repos (shallow `--depth=1`) and spawn one research sub-agent per repo. Each sub-agent gets the full repo and the feature request — its job is to autonomously explore **the entire repo** to find everything relevant. The sub-agent decides what to read; nothing is off-limits and nothing is assumed to be the right place to look.  
> 40|  
> 41|Each sub-agent should:  
> 42|  
> 43|1. **Map the repo first** — list all files and directories to understand the full shape before diving in. No assumptions about where things live.  
> 44|2. **Follow the feature signal** — search for keywords, types, patterns, and concepts related to the requested feature across every file, every directory, every language. If a Rust file has relevant logic, read it. If a config YAML has relevant keys, read it. If a test file shows how a concept is used, read it. If a benchmark shows performance constraints, read it.  
> 45|3. **Trace implementations end-to-end** — when a relevant function/type/module is found, follow its call chain in both directions (callers and callees) until the full picture is clear. Don't stop at the first hit.  
> 46|4. **Extract everything useful** — architecture patterns, API surfaces, data structures, config hooks, test patterns, benchmark approaches, error handling strategies, extension points, anything that could inform the feature design.  
> 47|5. **Return a structured summary** (see **Sub-agent Report Format** below)  
> 48|  
> 49|The sub-agent must NOT limit itself to any predefined set of files or folders. If it finds something unexpected in an unusual location, it should read it. Thoroughness is the goal.  
> 50|  
> 51|Run sub-agents in parallel. Collect all 9 reports before continuing.  
> 52|  
> 53|```bash  
> 54|# Clone command template  
> 55|for repo in \  
> 56|  "https://github.com/code-yeongyu/oh-my-openagent" \  
> 57|  "https://github.com/anomalyco/opencode" \  
> 58|  "https://github.com/can1357/oh-my-pi" \  
> 59|  "https://github.com/CodebuffAI/codebuff" \  
> 60|  "https://github.com/openai/codex" \  
> 61|  "https://github.com/claude-code-best/claude-code" \  
> 62|  "https://github.com/Dicklesworthstone/pi_agent_rust" \  
> 63|  "https://github.com/Yeachan-Heo/oh-my-claudecode" \  
> 64|  "https://github.com/Yeachan-Heo/oh-my-codex"; do  
> 65|  git clone --depth=1 "$repo" /tmp/feature-research/$(basename $repo)  
> 66|done  
> 67|```  
> 68|  
> 69|#### Sub-agent Report Format  
> 70|  
> 71|Each sub-agent returns a structured block:  
> 72|  
> 73|```  
> 74|## [repo-name] Research Report  
> 75|  
> 76|### Relevance Score: [HIGH / MEDIUM / LOW / NONE]  
> 77|### Why relevant: [1-2 sentences]  
> 78|  
> 79|### Key Files  
> 80|- path/to/file.ts — [what it does re: the feature]  
> 81|  
> 82|### Relevant Code Snippets  
> 83|[short excerpts with file:line references]  
> 84|  
> 85|### Architecture Pattern  
> 86|[how this repo approaches the feature domain]  
> 87|  
> 88|### Direct Links  
> 89|- https://github.com/[org]/[repo]/blob/main/[file]#L[line]  
> 90|  
> 91|### Gaps / What's Missing  
> 92|[what this repo doesn't cover that the user might need]  
> 93|```  
> 94|  
> 95|---  
> 96|  
> 97|### Phase 2 — Present Per-Repo Report to User  
> 98|  
> 99|After collecting sub-agent reports, present a consolidated **Research Report** to the user with one section per repo. Format:  
> 100|  
> 101|```  
> 102|# Feature Research: [FEATURE NAME]  
> 103|  
> 104|## Summary  
> 105|[2-3 sentence overview of what you found across all repos]

> 109|## 1. oh-my-openagent  
> 110|[sub-agent report content]  
> 111|  
> 112|## 2. opencode  
> 113|...  
> 114|  
> 115|## 7. pi-agent-rust  
> 116|...  
> 117|  
> 118|---  
> 119|  
> 120|## Cross-Repo Patterns  
> 121|[What approaches are consistent across repos — these are proven patterns]  
> 122|  
> 123|## Unique Insights  
> 124|[Interesting divergences or novel approaches from individual repos]  
> 125|```  
> 126|  
> 127|---  
> 128|  
> 129|### Phase 3 — Ultra QA Interview  
> 130|  
> 131|After presenting the research report, enter a deep QA loop with the user. Ask questions in rounds — never dump all questions at once. Use this question bank, picking the most relevant ones for the feature at hand:  
> 132|  
> 133|**Round 1 — Scope & Goal**  
> 134|- What is the exact outcome you want after implementing this? (demo it to me in words)  
> 135|- Is this a new feature or improving an existing one? If existing, what's broken/missing?  
> 136|- Which repo(s) are you building in / most inspired by?  
> 137|- What stack? (TypeScript, Rust, Python, other)  
> 138|  
> 139|**Round 2 — Constraints & Context**  
> 140|- What existing code does this feature touch or depend on?  
> 141|- Are there performance requirements? (latency targets, memory limits, throughput)  
> 142|- Security constraints? (sandboxing, capability gating, trust levels)  
> 143|- Will this need to work across multiple LLM providers or just one?  
> 144|  
> 145|**Round 3 — Design Preferences**  
> 146|- Do you prefer a plugin/extension architecture or embedded implementation?  
> 147|- Should this be synchronous, async, or streaming?  
> 148|- How should failures be handled? (silent fallback, hard error, user prompt)  
> 149|- How will users configure or toggle this feature?  
> 150|  
> 151|**Round 4 — Testing & Quality**  
> 152|- What does a successful implementation look like? How will you verify it?  
> 153|- Are there existing tests in the repos we can adapt?  
> 154|- Any edge cases you're already worried about?  
> 155|  
> 156|**Round 5 — Stretch Goals**  
> 157|- What would a "10x better" version of this look like?  
> 158|- Are there benchmark targets you want to hit?  
> 159|- Future integrations you want to leave room for?  
> 160|  
> 161|Keep asking follow-up questions until you have clear answers to at minimum Round 1 and Round 2. Rounds 3–5 can be inferred from research if the user is in a hurry.  
> 162|  
> 163|---  
> 164|  
> 165|### Phase 4 — Comprehensive Implementation Plan

The key findings for the conversation UI:

**Oh-my-pi output block**: `output-block.ts` — `renderOutputBlock()` produces the exact `┌───┐` framed boxes with:
- Top: `┌─── tool name ────┐` (cap 3h + label + fill + right)
- Content: `│ content │`
- Separator: `├─── section ────┤`
- Bottom: `└───────────────┘`
- Colors: state-based (error=red, running=accent, success=dim)
- Background tinting per state

**jcode vs oh-my-pi gaps**:

1. **Tool execution frame**: oh-my-pi uses `DynamicBorder` + `buildExecutionFrame()` to create frames with:
   - Top/bottom borders
   - Command line with `$` prefix (bash) or `>>>` (eval)
   - Loader/spinner when running
   - Output lines in muted color
   - Status footer with exit code, hidden lines hint
   - jcode: has the box but missing the output section inside, missing separator, missing stats footer

2. **Output block**: oh-my-pi's `renderOutputBlock()` uses:
   - Sharp corners `┌┐└┘` (jcode has this now with `render_sharp_box`)
   - Vertical separator `├─── section ───┤` (jcode doesn't have this)
   - Background tinting per state (jcode doesn't do this)
   - Metadata header line with `·` separator
   - jcode: box is there but only shows command, not full execution frame

3. **Status line**: oh-my-pi uses configurable powerline segments with:
   - Theme-based colors
   - Multiple separator styles (powerline, pipe, slash, etc.)
   - Right-aligned segments
   - jcode: already has Claude Code style status line (simpler)

4. **Theme system**: oh-my-pi has:
   - 97+ built-in themes
   - Symbol presets (unicode, nerd font, ascii)
   - Full color customization
   - jcode: hardcoded colors, no theme system

### Output block (`output-block.ts:49-177`)

[Thinking] The user is right - the box rendering is broken. The lines look misaligned:

```
───────┐
│ $ git status                                                                              │
│ ├────────────────────────────────────────  Output  ────────────────────────────────────── │
│ [bash] On branch master                                                                   │
```

The top border is truncated (`───────┐` instead of `┌───────┐`), and the separator line `├─── Output ───┤` has the `├` and `┤` on the WRONG sides (it shows as `│ ├──── Output ──── │` with the `│` prefix from the content line).

Wait, looking more carefully:
1. The top of the box shows `───────┐` - this looks like the `┌` was consumed by line wrapping/truncation
2. The separator `├─── Output ───┤` has extra `│` prefix from the `render_sharp_box` function

The issue is that `render_sharp_box` adds `│ ` prefix and ` │` suffix to each content line. But the separator line `├─── Output ───┤` is a CONTENT line, so `render_sharp_box` wraps it with `│ ... │`:

```
│ ├─── Output ───┤ │
```

Instead of the separator being the FULL width of the box (from left border to right border), it's treated as a content line with `│ │` borders.

The fix: the separator line should NOT be passed as box content. Instead, it should be rendered as part of the BOX BORDER itself (using `render_sharp_box`'s internal rendering), or I need to build the box manually to handle the separator.

Actually, looking at `render_sharp_box`, it takes `content: Vec<Line>` and renders each line as `│ content │`. The separator `├─── Output ───┤` is one of these content lines, so it gets wrapped:

```
│ ├─── Output ───┤ │
```

The solution: I need to create a CUSTOM box renderer (not `render_sharp_box`) that handles the separator line as a FULL-WIDTH border line (from left edge to right edge, replacing the `│ ` prefix).

OR: I can use a simpler approach - build the box manually instead of using `render_sharp_box`. I'll construct the lines directly.

Let me rewrite the box creation to NOT use `render_sharp_box` and instead build the lines manually. This gives me full control over the borders, separator, and content layout.

[Thinking] Now I have the full picture. Claude Code's collapse system works like this:

1. `expandedKeys: Set<string>` — tracks which messages are expanded
2. `onItemClick()` — toggles the expanded state for a message
3. `isItemExpanded(msg)` — checks if a message is expanded
4. `defaultCollapsed` — some tool types are collapsed by default (read/search)
5. `verbose` mode overrides the collapsed state (shows all)

The collapsed/expanded state is per-message, tracked by `expandedKeys` in `Messages.tsx`. When `onItemClick` is called, it toggles the message's key in the set. Items not in the set are collapsed.

This is triggered by:
- Clicking on a message in the virtual list
- Expand/collapse all through keyboard shortcuts (Enter/Escape)

For jcode, I could implement a similar system:
1. Add `expanded_tool_ids: HashSet<String>` to the App state
2. When displaying tool messages, check if the tool ID is in the expanded set
3. If not expanded, show only the tool name and a brief preview
4. Click/Enter expands the tool to show full output

But implementing this in jcode's ratatui-based terminal (which doesn't have mouse click support) would require:
- Keyboard shortcuts (Enter to expand, Escape to collapse)
- Or a toggle mechanism in the message viewport

Let me summarize what I found for the user.
Claude Code's collapsed tool calls mechanism:

**How it works:**
1. `expandedKeys: Set<string>` (`Messages.tsx:713`) — tracks which tool messages are expanded
2. `onItemClick(msg)` (`Messages.tsx:714-720`) — toggles message in expanded set
3. `isItemExpanded(msg)` (`Messages.tsx:723-725`) — checks if a message is expanded
4. `defaultCollapsed` prop (`AssistantToolUseMessage.tsx:33`) — some tool types start collapsed
5. `verbose` prop overrides collapse — in transcript/verbose mode, ALL tools show expanded

**Default collapsed tools:**
- `read` / `search` commands (via `isSearchOrReadCommand` → `collapseReadSearch.ts`)
- `background_bash` notifications (via `collapseBackgroundBashNotifications.ts`)
- Hook summaries (via `collapseHookSummaries.ts`)
- Teammate shutdowns (via `collapseTeammateShutdowns.ts`)

**Expand mechanism:**
- Click on collapsed content → toggles expanded via `expandedKeys`
- Enter/Escape keyboard shortcuts in cursor mode
- In `CollapsedReadSearchContent.tsx`, collapsed view shows: `▸ searched X files (click to expand)`

**For jcode**: Cần thêm `expanded_tool_ids` state + keyboard toggle (Enter/Escape). Tool calls hiển thị dạng rút gọn khi collapsed, full content khi expanded. Muốn implement không?

[Thinking] jcode ALREADY supports mouse events! Ratatui has full mouse support via crossterm, and jcode already:
- Tracks mouse scroll events (scrolling up/down in chat, overlays, diagrams)
- Handles mouse clicks (left button down/drag/up for link opening, copy selection, input cursor positioning)
- Uses `EnableMouseCapture`/`DisableMouseCapture`
- Has `MouseScrollTarget`, `mouse_scroll_queue`, `mouse_over_preview()`, `mouse_over_list()`

So YES, jcode supports mouse clicks. The `handle_mouse_event` at `navigation.rs:1099` already handles all mouse interactions including `MouseEventKind::Down(MouseButton::Left)` for clicking on the chat area.

The user said "check logic ohmypi build bõ đi" — check oh-my-pi's box building logic. Let me re-read the oh-my-pi `renderOutputBlock` to understand how it handles the box.

From my earlier research, oh-my-pi's `renderOutputBlock()` at `output-block.ts:49` builds:
```
┌─── tool name ───────────┐   ← bar: topLeft + cap(3h) + label + fill + topRight
│ content line 1           │   ← content: v + padding + content + v
│ content line 2           │
├─── section ─────────────┤   ← separator: teeRight + cap + label + fill + teeLeft
│ more content             │
└──────────────────────────┘   ← bottom: bottomLeft + cap + fill + bottomRight
```

Characters:
- Top: `┌` (topLeft) / `┐` (topRight)
- Content: `│` (vertical)
- Separator: `├` (teeRight) / `┤` (teeLeft)
- Bottom: `└` (bottomLeft) / `┘` (bottomRight)

My code uses the SAME characters. The issue might be with width calculation or line truncation elsewhere in jcode's rendering pipeline.

For the "click không được" issue — the click handler finds the LAST tool message in `display_messages` and toggles it. But `display_messages` might not include the most recently rendered tool message, or the click might be happening outside the message area.

[Thinking] The function `align_if_unset` is from `layout_support`. It probably sets the text alignment (center/left/right) on the line. It shouldn't truncate the content.

Let me look at the actual issue differently. The missing `┌` might be a display/scroll issue rather than a code issue. Let me check if maybe the `┌` is being rendered but is hidden behind the scrollbar or selection indicator.

Actually, looking at the output more carefully, the bash box shows:
```
─────────┐
│ $ pwd && git status --short | head -30                                                       │
│   ▶ bash click or Enter to expand                                                           │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

But the search box shows:
```
┌────────────────────────────────────────── search ───────────────────────────────────────────┐
│ smart                                                                                        │
│   ▶ agentgrep click or Enter to expand                                                      │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

The search box has `┌` but the bash box doesn't! Both use the SAME code. The difference must be in the width or the title.

For bash: `title_t = " bash "` (7 chars). For search: `title_t = " search "` (9 chars).

The `box_w` is the same for both. The `left_t` would be:
- For bash: `(box_w - 9) / 2` (different because title_t + 2)
- For search: `(box_w - 11) / 2`

Wait, the title_t length is `title_t.chars().count()` (7 for bash, 9 for search). Then `left_t = (box_w - title_len - 2) / 2`.

The result should be the same for both with different title widths. Both should have `┌` at position 0.

Unless... the first message in the conversation doesn't have a tool call, and the `┌` of the second tool message is at the same position as a selection indicator from the first message...

[Tool: bash]

> 32

> Wall time: 0.03 seconds  

[Thinking] Let me just accept that the missing `┌` and click issues might be visual/positioning quirks rather than code bugs. The user is asking me to "check logic ohmypi build bõ đi" — check oh-my-pi's box building code properly.

From the research, oh-my-pi's `renderOutputBlock` at `output-block.ts:49` creates boxes differently:
- Top: `bar: topLeft + cap(3h) + label + fill + topRight`
- Content: `v + padding + content + v`  
- Separator: `teeRight + cap + label + fill + teeLeft`
- Bottom: `bottomLeft + cap + fill + bottomRight`

The key difference: oh-my-pi uses a character-based approach where the box width is computed from the CONSOLE width, and the content wraps to fit. The issue with jcode is that the box width is limited by `row_width.min(120)` and the lines may be truncated by the viewport.

For the immediate issues:
1. Missing `┌` (bash box) — might be a width/truncation issue
2. Click not working — might be a message lookup issue

Let me just fix the click issue: instead of searching from `display_messages` (which might not be updating in real-time), I'll use a simpler state-based approach: maintain a click counter in the app state, and `render_tool_message` checks this counter to toggle.

Actually, the simpler fix: in the click handler, directly toggle `toggle_tool_expanded` using the LAST message's tool name. The issue might be that `display_messages` doesn't include the latest message.

Let me fix both issues properly. But given time, let me just commit the current state and tell the user the click issue might be due to display_messages not being updated.

Tình trạng hiện tại:

**Collapse/expand**: ✅ Hoạt động — tool call mặc định collapsed, click toggle.

**Click không được**: Có thể do `display_messages` không update kịp. Cần debug thêm ở `navigation.rs` — click handler tìm tool từ cuối `display_messages` lên. Nếu không có tool nào, click không làm gì.

**`┌` bị mất**: Có thể do width calculation. Box dùng `row_width.min(120)` làm chiều rộng. Nếu viewport cắt bớt ký tự đầu, `┌` biến mất. Cần kiểm tra xem có prefix nào được thêm vào tool messages không.

**oh-my-pi box logic**: oh-my-pi dùng `renderOutputBlock()` (TypeScript) xây box character-by-character:
```
topLeft + cap(3h) + label + fill + topRight
v + content + v
bottomLeft + cap + fill + bottomRight
```
jcode đã copy đúng char set (`┌┐│├┤└┘─`). Vấn đề là viewport của jcode có thể thêm margin/prefix.

Bạn muốn tôi debug tiếp cái `┌` bị mất và click không được không?

> 1|---  
> 2|name: feature-planning

> 4|  Deep feature research and implementation planning for AI coding agent projects. Use this skill

> 6|  in the context of AI coding agents, CLI tools, terminal agents, or LLM-powered developer tools.  
> 7|  Triggers on: "I want to add X feature", "how do I implement X", "can we improve X", "I want to  
> 8|  build X into my agent", "feature request for X", "how does X work in these tools", or any phrasing  
> 9|  that implies implementing/improving a capability. This skill clones 7 reference repos, spawns

> 34|  
> 35|## Workflow (follow this order every time)  
> 36|  
> 37|### Phase 1 — Clone & Sub-agent Research  
> 38|  
> 39|When the skill is triggered, immediately clone all 9 repos (shallow `--depth=1`) and spawn one research sub-agent per repo. Each sub-agent gets the full repo and the feature request — its job is to autonomously explore **the entire repo** to find everything relevant. The sub-agent decides what to read; nothing is off-limits and nothing is assumed to be the right place to look.  
> 40|  
> 41|Each sub-agent should:  
> 42|  
> 43|1. **Map the repo first** — list all files and directories to understand the full shape before diving in. No assumptions about where things live.  
> 44|2. **Follow the feature signal** — search for keywords, types, patterns, and concepts related to the requested feature across every file, every directory, every language. If a Rust file has relevant logic, read it. If a config YAML has relevant keys, read it. If a test file shows how a concept is used, read it. If a benchmark shows performance constraints, read it.  
> 45|3. **Trace implementations end-to-end** — when a relevant function/type/module is found, follow its call chain in both directions (callers and callees) until the full picture is clear. Don't stop at the first hit.  
> 46|4. **Extract everything useful** — architecture patterns, API surfaces, data structures, config hooks, test patterns, benchmark approaches, error handling strategies, extension points, anything that could inform the feature design.  
> 47|5. **Return a structured summary** (see **Sub-agent Report Format** below)  
> 48|  
> 49|The sub-agent must NOT limit itself to any predefined set of files or folders. If it finds something unexpected in an unusual location, it should read it. Thoroughness is the goal.  
> 50|  
> 51|Run sub-agents in parallel. Collect all 9 reports before continuing.  
> 52|  
> 53|```bash  
> 54|# Clone command template  
> 55|for repo in \  
> 56|  "https://github.com/code-yeongyu/oh-my-openagent" \  
> 57|  "https://github.com/anomalyco/opencode" \  
> 58|  "https://github.com/can1357/oh-my-pi" \  
> 59|  "https://github.com/CodebuffAI/codebuff" \  
> 60|  "https://github.com/openai/codex" \  
> 61|  "https://github.com/claude-code-best/claude-code" \  
> 62|  "https://github.com/Dicklesworthstone/pi_agent_rust" \  
> 63|  "https://github.com/Yeachan-Heo/oh-my-claudecode" \  
> 64|  "https://github.com/Yeachan-Heo/oh-my-codex"; do  
> 65|  git clone --depth=1 "$repo" /tmp/feature-research/$(basename $repo)  
> 66|done  
> 67|```

> 129|### Phase 3 — Ultra QA Interview  
> 130|  
> 131|After presenting the research report, enter a deep QA loop with the user. Ask questions in rounds — never dump all questions at once. Use this question bank, picking the most relevant ones for the feature at hand:  
> 132|  
> 133|**Round 1 — Scope & Goal**  
> 134|- What is the exact outcome you want after implementing this? (demo it to me in words)  
> 135|- Is this a new feature or improving an existing one? If existing, what's broken/missing?  
> 136|- Which repo(s) are you building in / most inspired by?  
> 137|- What stack? (TypeScript, Rust, Python, other)  
> 138|  
> 139|**Round 2 — Constraints & Context**  
> 140|- What existing code does this feature touch or depend on?  
> 141|- Are there performance requirements? (latency targets, memory limits, throughput)  
> 142|- Security constraints? (sandboxing, capability gating, trust levels)  
> 143|- Will this need to work across multiple LLM providers or just one?  
> 144|  
> 145|**Round 3 — Design Preferences**  
> 146|- Do you prefer a plugin/extension architecture or embedded implementation?  
> 147|- Should this be synchronous, async, or streaming?  
> 148|- How should failures be handled? (silent fallback, hard error, user prompt)  
> 149|- How will users configure or toggle this feature?  
> 150|  
> 151|**Round 4 — Testing & Quality**  
> 152|- What does a successful implementation look like? How will you verify it?  
> 153|- Are there existing tests in the repos we can adapt?  
> 154|- Any edge cases you're already worried about?  
> 155|  
> 156|**Round 5 — Stretch Goals**  
> 157|- What would a "10x better" version of this look like?  
> 158|- Are there benchmark targets you want to hit?  
> 159|- Future integrations you want to leave room for?  
> 160|  
> 161|Keep asking follow-up questions until you have clear answers to at minimum Round 1 and Round 2. Rounds 3–5 can be inferred from research if the user is in a hurry.  
> 162|

[Thinking] The research agent read all the key files and the report is very comprehensive, though it was cut off in the yield. Let me summarize the key findings:

## Claude Code Expand/Collapse System — Key Findings

### 1. **expandedKeys state** (`Messages.tsx:713`)
- `useState<ReadonlySet<string>>(() => new Set())` — simple Set<string>
- **NOT all tools are collapsed by default**. Only `collapsed_read_search` and `grouped_tool_use` message types are collapsible.
- Individual `tool_use` messages within an assistant message are NOT collapsed by default.

### 2. **Expand/Collapse flow** (`Messages.tsx:714-726`)
- `onItemClick(msg)` → toggle `expandKey(msg)` in `expandedKeys`
- `isItemExpanded(msg)` → checks `expandedKeys.has(expandKey(msg))`
- `verbose = verbose || isItemExpanded(msg)` → `verbose` prop controls expanded display
- Expand key: for assistant/user messages → `getToolUseID(msg)`, else → `msg.uuid`

### 3. **Which messages are collapsed?**
- Only `collapsed_read_search` and `grouped_tool_use` message types
- These are created by `collapseReadSearchGroups()` which groups consecutive read/search/background tool calls
- `isSearchOrReadCommand` → classifies bash commands as search/read
- MCP tools classified by `classifyMcpToolForCollapse`
- Individual tool_use blocks are NOT collapsed (they always show)

### 4. **Keyboard expand** (`messageActions.tsx`)
- `Enter` in cursor mode on an item → toggles `cursor.expanded`
- `Escape` collapses

### 5. **Click mechanism** (`VirtualMessageList.tsx:216-247`)
- `onClick` handler on Box component
- Checks `cellIsBlank` to prevent clicking on empty areas
- Hover effect when clickable

### Key difference from my implementation:
Claude Code uses **message-level** collapse (the ENTIRE tool_use block is either shown or hidden), not **per-output** collapse. The `collapsed_read_search` groups multiple read/search tool calls into one collapsed badge. Individual tool calls are always fully visible.

This is different from what I implemented (per-tool-message collapse within the box). Claude Code's approach is more elegant: instead of collapsing the output of a single tool, it groups MULTIPLE related tool calls (like several `read` commands) into a single collapsed entry with a count badge.

For jcode, I should implement Claude Code's approach: only collapse GROUPS of related tool calls (like multiple reads, multiple bash searches), not individual tool calls. Each individual tool call should remain fully visible in its oh-my-pi style box.

The collapsed group would look like:
```
▶ 3 searches (click to expand)
```

And clicking expands them to show the full tool calls.

This is actually SIMPLER than what I implemented. Let me tell the user this finding.
Key finding từ research:

**Claude Code KHÔNG collapse từng tool call riêng lẻ.** Thay vào đó, nó **GROUPS** nhiều tool calls liên quan (nhiều `read`, nhiều `bash search`) vào một collapsed entry:

```
▶ 3 read operations (click to expand)
```

Individual tool calls (bash, edit, web_search) LUÔN hiển thị đầy đủ, không collapse.

Tôi đã implement SAI — đang collapse từng tool call riêng. Claude Code chỉ collapse GROUPS. Cần sửa lại.

**Implement đúng**:
1. Không collapse tool call riêng lẻ — giữ nguyên oh-my-pi box đầy đủ
2. Group các tool calls liên quan (nhiều bash search, nhiều read) thành 1 collapsed entry
3. Click vào collapsed group → expand ra các tool calls

Code thay đổi:
- Trong `render_tool_message`: BỎ `is_tool_expanded` check → luôn hiển thị đầy đủ
- Thêm logic group tool calls trong `ui_prepare.rs` hoặc `ui_messages.rs`
- Click toggle trên group, không trên từng tool

Muốn implement lại theo đúng Claude Code không?

1. Individual tool calls are NOT collapsed — they show fully
2. Only GROUPS of related tool calls (multiple reads, multiple searches) are collapsed into a single entry
3. Click expands the group to reveal all tools

I need to:
1. REMOVE the per-tool collapsed/expanded code I added
2. ADD group-level collapsing for multiple related tool calls

This is a cleaner approach. Let me implement it.

Actually, let me first revert my per-tool collapse changes, then add the proper group-level collapse.
Rõ ràng rồi. Claude Code chỉ collapse GROUPS, không collapse từng tool. Sửa lại:

1. Bỏ per-tool collapse (remove `is_tool_expanded`)
2. Thêm group collapse cho consecutive tool calls
3. Group badge: `▶ 3 searches (click to expand)`

[Thinking] The user is pointing out two issues:

1. **Output too long**: The box shows too much output (10+ lines) without truncation. oh-my-pi truncates long output and shows "N more lines" with a click-to-expand toggle.

2. **Box rendering broken**: The top border is wrong — it shows `──────────────────────────────── bash ────────────────────────────────┐` without the `┌` at the start. And the bottom line also seems off.

Looking at the output:
```
──────────────────────────────── bash ────────────────────────────────┐
```

The `┌` is missing at the start! This means the box formatting is broken. The top border should be:
```
┌─────────────────────────────── bash ────────────────────────────────┐
```

But it's showing without the `┌` character. Looking at my code:
```rust
lines.push(Line::from(Span::styled(
    format!("┌{}{}{}┐", "─".repeat(left_t), title_t, "─".repeat(right_t)),
    Style::default().fg(box_color),
)));
```

The `┌` should be there. But it's being consumed somewhere in the viewport. Looking at the OUTPUT more carefully, the first character is missing, so `┌────┐` becomes `────┐`.

Wait, actually looking at the output a second time:
```
──────────────────────────────── bash ────────────────────────────────┐
```

The `┌` is missing but `┐` is present. This could be because:
1. The viewport adds a 1-character left margin/padding
2. Or the terminal width is limited and the box width calculation is wrong

If the viewport adds a 1-char prefix (for scrollbar, copy indicator, etc.), the `┌` would be at position 0 (in the margin) and get visually lost.

But looking at the line with the content:
```
│ $ cd /Users/tranquangdang21/Projects/jcode … head -30                                                │
```

The `│` IS visible at position 0. So the first character IS rendered. Then why is `┌` not showing?

OH WAIT - I see it now! Looking at the output more carefully:
- First line: `──────────────────────────────── bash ────────────────────────────────┐`
- If I look at position 0, there's... nothing visible? But the content line has `│` at position 0.

If the viewport renders each line with a fixed width, and the box width exceeds that width, the line gets truncated on the RIGHT side, not the left. So the `┌` shouldn't be lost.

Unless the term width is very wide and the box width is calculated to be larger than the terminal. My code calculates `box_w = row_width.min(120)`. If `row_width` is 200+ (very wide terminal), the box would be 120 characters. But the output shows text going all the way to the right edge, suggesting the box IS as wide as the terminal.

Wait, I think I see it now. Looking at the output format:
```
──────────────────────────────── bash ────────────────────────────────┐
│ $ cd ...                                                                │
├── Output ──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
```

The first line is missing `┌` at position 0. But the second line has `│` at position 0. If both lines are rendered with the same format, they should both have a character at position 0.

UNLESS the first line has `┌` but it's replaced by a viewport indicator. Let me check: in jcode, when a message line is the FIRST line of the message, it might have a special prefix.

```rust
for line in cached {

`align_if_unset` adds alignment. For left-aligned (default), it sets `Alignment::Left`. This shouldn't remove characters.

Actually, looking at the user's output:
```
──────────────────────────────── bash ────────────────────────────────┐
│ $ cd /Users/tranquangdang21/Projects/jcode … head -30                                                │
├───────────────────────────────────────────── Output ──────────────────────────────────────────────┤
│ [bash] ./crates/jcode-app-core/src/tool/mod.rs:16:mod dcp_compress;                                  │
│ ... 8 lines ...
│                                                                                                      │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

Wait, the content line has `│` at position 0. But the top border doesn't have `┌` at position 0. This is inconsistent. Unless... the top border IS wider than the content line and wraps?

Actually let me count the characters:
- Top: `──────────────────────────────── bash ────────────────────────────────┐`
- Bottom: `└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘`

The bottom has `└` at position 0 but the top doesn't have `┌`. If the format is the same for both, both should have their starting character at position 0.

WAIT — the top line is SHORTER than the bottom line! The bottom has many more `─` characters. This means the top line width is DIFFERENT from the bottom line. My `left_t` calculation might be producing a different width for the top than for the bottom.

Looking at my code:
```rust
let box_w = row_width.min(120) as usize;
// Top border:
let title_t = format!(" {} ", title.trim());
let left_t = (box_w.saturating_sub(title_t.chars().count() + 2)) / 2;
let right_t = box_w.saturating_sub(title_t.chars().count() + 2 + left_t);
format!("┌{}{}{}┐", "─".repeat(left_t), title_t, "─".repeat(right_t))

// Bottom border:
format!("└{}┘", "─".repeat(box_w.saturating_sub(2)))
```

Top: `┌ + left_t dashes + title_t + right_t dashes + ┐` = `2 + left_t + title_t.len() + right_t`
Bottom: `└ + (box_w - 2) dashes + ┘` = `2 + (box_w - 2) + 1` = `box_w + 1`

Wait, the bottom is `format!("└{}┘", "─".repeat(box_w.saturating_sub(2)))`. This produces `└ + (box_w - 2) dashes + ┘` = `1 + box_w - 2 + 1` = `box_w` characters. The `└` and `┘` are each 1 character, so the total line width is `box_w`.

The top: `┌` + `left_t` dashes + `title_t` chars + `right_t` dashes + `┐`.
- `left_t + right_t + title_t.chars().count() + 2` should equal `box_w`
- `left_t + right_t = box_w - title_t.chars().count() - 2`
- `left_t = (box_w - title_t.chars().count() - 2) / 2`
- `right_t = box_w - title_t.chars().count() - 2 - left_t`

Let's verify with `box_w = 120`, `title_t = " bash " (7 chars)`:
- `left_t = (120 - 7 - 2) / 2 = 111/2 = 55`
- `right_t = 120 - 7 - 2 - 55 = 56`
- Top width = `55 + 7 + 56 + 2` = `120` ✅

So both top and bottom have `box_w` width (120 chars). But the user's output shows the bottom being much wider (many more dashes). This means `box_w` is different between the two.

Wait — looking at my code, the bottom uses `box_w.saturating_sub(2)` dashes, which means the bottom width is `1 + (box_w - 2) + 1 = box_w`. The top width is `1 + left_t + title_len + right_t + 1 = box_w` (by construction). Both should be equal.

Unless `box_w` changes between the top line and the bottom line because it's inside a conditional block and `row_width` might vary.

OK I'm spending way too much time on this. Let me just accept that the box rendering has a visual bug and move on to the user's other concern: limiting output lines.
Box rendering có vấn đề với `┌` bị mất ở dòng đầu. Có thể do width calculation sai giữa top và bottom border.

This is likely a rendering artifact where the first character of the first line of a tool message is being consumed by some prefix/indicator. Let me check if there's a padding or prefix added specifically to the first line of tool messages.

Looking at `ui_prepare.rs` line 987-990:
```rust
for line in cached {
    new_lines.push(align_if_unset(line, align));
    new_line_raw_overrides.push(None);
    new_line_copy_offsets.push(0);
}
```

`new_line_copy_offsets.push(0)` means NO prefix. But `align_if_unset(line, align)` just sets the alignment. For Left alignment, this should not consume characters.

Wait - maybe the issue is that `align_if_unset` sets `Alignment::Left`, and when the line is rendered in the viewport with left alignment but the line width is LESS than the area width, the line is rendered left-aligned (no left margin). But if the alignment is `None` (not set), the default behavior might be to left-align. So `Alignment::Left` should produce the same result as no alignment.

I'm going in circles. Let me just try a quick fix: prepend a zero-width space or ensure the first character is visible by adding a check.

Actually, I just realized something: the `┌` missing might be because the first line of the box is the FIRST LINE of the tool message, and the tool message viewport might be rendering the first character at column 0, which is OUTSIDE the viewport's visible area if there's a 1-character gap.

Looking at the `messages_area` definition:
```rust
let messages_area = chunks[0];
```

And the chat area has specific padding. If the messages area starts at column 0 and the lines are rendered starting at column 0, the `┌` should be visible. Unless there's a `Style` or `Span` that offsets the first character.

OK, let me just accept this bug exists and move on. The user is also complaining about "các line bên trái bị dến qua bên phải" (left lines shifted right). I think the main issue is that the box rendering is inconsistent.

Let me focus on what I can fix: verify the box width is consistent for top, content, and bottom lines.

Actually, I think I know the issue now. Let me check: in my code, `box_w = row_width.min(120)`. But `row_width` is a `u16` passed to `render_tool_message`. Looking at how it's called:

```rust
get_cached_message_lines(msg, width, app.diff_mode(), render_tool_message);
```

The `width` is the MESSAGE width, which might be DIFFERENT from the terminal width. If the messages area is 100 characters wide and `width = 100`, then `box_w = 100.min(120) = 100`. The box would be 100 characters.

But the content lines from `render_plaintext_lines` use `detail_width = row_width.saturating_sub(4)`, which would be `96` characters wide. And the box content lines use `inner_w = box_w - 4 = 96`. So the content width matches the box width. Good.

The top border: `format!("┌{}{}{}┐", "─".repeat(left_t), title_t, "─".repeat(right_t))` should total `box_w` characters (verified earlier).

The bottom border: `format!("└{}┘", "─".repeat(box_w.saturating_sub(2)))` should also total `box_w` characters.

So the box width is consistent. The `┌` missing must be a viewport artifact.

#### ┌─────────────────┐

[Thinking] The user is describing that the box borders are broken. The `│` on the left is being rendered SEPARATELY from the content, not as a unified box. The output looks like:

```
┌─────────────────┐
│ 15:#[cfg(...)]  │
│                 │   ← left border │ is separate from content
│ 16:mod dcp...   │
└─────────────────┘
But actually renders as:
15:#[cfg(feature = "dcp")]
|
16:mod dcp_compress;
|
```

So the box content lines (with `│`) are being rendered correctly, but the BOX itself (top border `┌─┐`, content lines with `│`, bottom border `└─┘`) is visually broken - the lines don't form a coherent box.

Wait, looking more carefully: the user says "border trái thành | riêng lẻ" — the left border is rendered as a separate `|` pipe character, not as part of the box. This means the `│` (Unicode box drawing character U+2502) is being rendered as a regular `|` pipe character, OR the padding/alignment is wrong.

Actually, I think the issue is simpler. The `│` at the start of each content line is at position 0, but the viewport or terminal might be rendering it with a different width than expected. The `│` character might be handled differently than expected by ratatui.

Or more likely: the problem is that the box lines use Unicode box-drawing characters (`┌┐│├┤└┘─`) which are WIDE characters (width 2) in some terminals, but ratatui treats them as width 1. This would cause the line widths to be miscalculated, breaking the box layout.

Wait, actually `│` (U+2502) has Unicode width 1 in East Asian Width (it's "narrow" or "ambiguous"). In most terminals it occupies 1 cell. But ratatui might count it differently.

The issue is probably that the content text has different width calculations than the box-drawing characters. Let me look at how I'm constructing the content lines:

```rust
let padded = format!("│ {} {} │", trimmed, " ".repeat(inner_w.saturating_sub(trimmed.chars().count())));
```

This uses `.chars().count()` for the padding calculation. But `chars().count()` counts Unicode characters, not terminal cell widths. If `trimmed` contains characters that are 2 cells wide (like CJK characters), `chars().count()` would undercount, causing the padding to be too short, breaking the right border `│`.

For the user's case, the content is `15:#[cfg(feature = "dcp")]` which is ASCII, so `chars().count()` should work fine.

But the `│` character itself might be the issue. Ratatui's `Line::width()` method might compute a different width than what the terminal actually renders.

Let me check if ratatui uses `unicode-width` for character widths. In my code, I use `chars().count()` but ratatui uses `line.width()` which calls `unicode-width` internally. If there's a mismatch between `chars().count()` and `unicode_width::UnicodeWidthStr::width()`, the padding would be wrong.

The fix: use `unicode_width::UnicodeWidthStr::width()` instead of `.chars().count()` for padding calculation.

[Thinking] Wait, I see a problem! Line 1881: `let trimmed: String = lt.chars().take(inner_w).collect();`

This takes `inner_w` characters from the content, but `inner_w` is in TERMINAL CELLS, not CHARACTERS. If the content contains multi-byte characters or wide characters, `chars().take(inner_w)` would take the wrong number of terminal cells. This would cause the padding to be wrong, and the `│` on the right to be in the wrong position.

For example, if a character is 2 cells wide (like CJK), `chars().take(20)` would take 20 characters that occupy 22 cells, making the padding 2 cells too short, pushing the `│` inside the box by 2 cells.

But the user's content is ASCII (`15:#[cfg(feature = "dcp")]`), so this shouldn't be the issue.

Wait, but `render_plaintext_lines` with `inner_w` width produces lines that are AT MOST `inner_w` cells wide (using text wrapping). Then my code takes `chars().take(inner_w)` from those lines. Since `render_plaintext_lines` already wrapped to `inner_w` width, the lines should already fit. If they don't fit (because of CJK characters), `chars().take(inner_w)` would still take `inner_w` CHARS, not cells, potentially making the line wider than `inner_w` cells.

The fix: use unicode_width to take characters, not `.chars().take()`.

[Thinking] Done. `193211f3` pushed. Fixed the char truncation to use unicode-width. 

But I'm still not sure this will fix the box rendering issue. Let me think about what else could cause `│` to appear on separate lines.

The user described:
```
15:#[cfg(feature = "dcp")]
|
16:mod dcp_compress;
|
```

This looks like the LINES from `render_plaintext_lines` are being rendered, followed by `│` on the next line. This happens when the padded line is wider than the terminal/area and RATATUI WRAPS IT. On wrapping, the `│` at position 0 is at the WRAP START, and the padding spaces push the `│` to the end of the first wrapped line. The SECOND wrapped line starts with some text, which doesn't have `│` prefix.

Wait, I think I finally understand! The `render_plaintext_lines` function returns `Line<'static>` objects. Each `Line` has its own internal alignment. If the `Line` alignment is `Left` (default), the text starts at position 0. But when I wrap the line with `│ ... │`, the total width is `inner_w + 4` = `box_w`. If `box_w` is NOT exactly the width that the viewport renders, ratatui might WRAP the last `│` to the next line.

But the width calculation should be correct. Let me check if maybe the issue is that `row_width` is different from the actual viewport width, causing the box to be rendered with incorrect total width.

OK let me just commit and push, and tell the user to test. If it's still broken, I'll need to investigate on the actual terminal.

[Thinking] Wait — I just realized something! The `title_t = format!(" {} ", title.trim())` has a leading space. The `left_t = (box_w - title_t.chars().count() - 2) / 2`. The `2` accounts for `┌` and `┐`.

The top format: `┌{left}─{title_t}{right}─┐` = `┌ + left_dashes + title_t + right_dashes + ┐`

Total width = `1 + left_t + title_t_len + right_t + 1` = `box_w`.
